                  <p></p>
                  </li>
               </ol>Furthermore, the Na-storage processes in Fe<sub>1-</sub><i><sub>x</sub></i>S@C-400 were further investigated by in situ Raman spectroscopy during the initial discharge–charge process, as presented in Figure&nbsp;<a href="#smll202312190-fig-0004">4c,d</a>. At the OCV≈2.5&nbsp;V, the two peaks at ≈287 and 370&nbsp;cm<sup>−1</sup> had been reported as characteristic bands of Fe<sub>1-</sub><i><sub>x</sub></i>S, which are consistent with the symmetric stretching vibrations of Fe─S and the longitudinal optical phonon vibration, respectively.<sup>[</sup><span><sup><a href="#smll202312190-bib-0045" class="bibLink tab-link" id="smll202312190-bib-0045_R_d30669543e1688" data-tab="pane-pcw-references" aria-label="Reference 45 - Microsyst. Nanoeng.">45</a>, <a href="#smll202312190-bib-0046" class="bibLink tab-link" id="smll202312190-bib-0046_R_d30669543e1688" data-tab="pane-pcw-references" aria-label="Reference 46 - J. Raman Spectrosc.">46</a></sup></span><sup>]</sup> The intensity of the peaks gradually decreased during the sodiation process.<sup>[</sup><span><sup><a href="#smll202312190-bib-0047" class="bibLink tab-link" id="smll202312190-bib-0047_R_d30669543e1693" data-tab="pane-pcw-references" aria-label="Reference 47 - RSC Adv.">47</a></sup></span><sup>]</sup> When the cell was discharged to 0.01&nbsp;V for complete breaking, the Fe─S peak disappeared, indicating that Fe<sub>1-</sub><i><sub>x</sub></i>S reacted with Na and converted into Fe and Na<sub>2</sub>S. when recharged back to 3.0&nbsp;V, two weak broad peaks appeared again at ≈290 and 373&nbsp;cm<sup>−1</sup>, indicating the formation of Fe<sub>1-</sub><i><sub>x</sub></i>S, which was consistent with that of in situ XRD data. The formation of Fe<sub>1-</sub><i><sub>x</sub></i>S after fully charged indicated that the ultrafine pulverization of the Fe<sub>1-</sub><i><sub>x</sub></i>S@C composite overcame the significant kinetic and thermodynamic constraints of electrochemical conversion reactions.<sup>[</sup><span><sup><a href="#smll202312190-bib-0018" class="bibLink tab-link" id="smll202312190-bib-0018_R_d30669543e1720" data-tab="pane-pcw-references" aria-label="Reference 18 - ACS Nano">18</a></sup></span><sup>]</sup> This remarkable result can be attributed to the size of pulverized nanoparticles, which are ≈5&nbsp;nm or less, making them comparable to or even smaller than the diffusion distance of iron during cation exchange. As a result, these nanoparticles can offer thermodynamically reversible nanodomains for the conversion reaction of metallic Fe and Na<sub>2</sub>S.<sup>[</sup><span><sup><a href="#smll202312190-bib-0018" class="bibLink tab-link" id="smll202312190-bib-0018_R_d30669543e1728" data-tab="pane-pcw-references" aria-label="Reference 18 - ACS Nano">18</a></sup></span><sup>]</sup> This finding demonstrates that the sluggish reaction kinetics of sulfur and Na<sub>2</sub>S can be effectively improved by ultrafine pulverization, leading to a significant enhancement in specific capacity and cycling stability. The electrochemical reaction mechanism is summarized in Figure&nbsp;<a href="#smll202312190-fig-0004">4e</a>. Furthermore, the graphitization degree of the Fe<sub>1-</sub><i><sub>x</sub></i>S@C-400 composite was also investigated by ex situ Raman during the initial cycle. Figure <a class="suppLink scrollableLink" href="#support-information-section">S11</a> (Supporting Information), exhibited the graphitization degree of carbon materials (I<sub>D</sub>/I<sub>G</sub>) in Fe<sub>1-</sub><i><sub>x</sub></i>S@C-400 composite continues to decrease as the cycle proceeds, indicating abundant defects, vacancies, and a higher degree of disorder. It should be pointed out that the highly disordered structure would be more beneficial to offer extra active sites for large sodium ions storage.<sup>[</sup><span><sup><a href="#smll202312190-bib-0048" class="bibLink tab-link" id="smll202312190-bib-0048_R_d30669543e1754" data-tab="pane-pcw-references" aria-label="Reference 48 - Adv. Energy Mater.">48</a></sup></span><sup>]</sup></div>
         
         <section class="article-section__inline-figure">
            <figure class="figure" id="smll202312190-fig-0004"><a target="_blank" href="/cms/asset/2897027d-237d-419b-bfdb-49348c64d1ac/smll202312190-fig-0004-m.jpg"><picture>
                     <source srcset="/cms/asset/2897027d-237d-419b-bfdb-49348c64d1ac/smll202312190-fig-0004-m.jpg" media="(min-width: 1650px)"><img class="figure__image" src="/cms/asset/561186ac-fe8f-45a5-80ed-c1d5f9f67560/smll202312190-fig-0004-m.png" data-lg-src="/cms/asset/2897027d-237d-419b-bfdb-49348c64d1ac/smll202312190-fig-0004-m.jpg" alt="Details are in the caption following the image" title="Details are in the caption following the image" loading="lazy"></picture></a><figcaption class="figure__caption">
                  <div class="figure__caption__header"><strong class="figure__title">Figure 4<span style="font-weight:normal"></span></strong><div class="figure-extra"><a href="#" class="open-figure-link">Open in figure viewer</a><a href="/action/downloadFigures?id=smll202312190-fig-0004&amp;partId=&amp;doi=10.1002%2Fsmll.202312190" class="ppt-figure-link"><i aria-hidden="true" class="icon-Icon_Download"></i><span>PowerPoint</span></a></div>
                  </div>
                  <div class="figure__caption figure__caption-text">In situ XRD and Raman analysis of Fe<sub>1-</sub><i><sub>x</sub></i>S@C-400 electrode and reaction mechanism. a) Contour plots of in situ XRD results of Fe<sub>1-</sub><i><sub>x</sub></i>S@C-400 electrode against the voltage profile during the initial cycle at a cutoff voltage of 0.01–3.0&nbsp;V; b) Corresponding in situ XRD patterns of Fe<sub>1-</sub><i><sub>x</sub></i>S@C-400 electrode and corresponding initial discharge and charge profiles of Fe<sub>1-</sub><i><sub>x</sub></i>S@C-400 electrode; c,d) Stacked in situ Raman patterns of Fe<sub>1-</sub><i><sub>x</sub></i>S@C-400 electrode during the initial discharge–charge process at different voltages; e) Schematic illustration for the Na storage mechanism of Fe<sub>1-</sub><i><sub>x</sub></i>S during the initial discharge–charge process.</div>
               </figcaption>
            </figure>
         </section>
         <div class="paragraph-element">To understand the excellent rate capability of Fe<sub>1-</sub><i><sub>x</sub></i>S@C-400 anode in SIBs, the kinetics of Fe<sub>1-</sub><i><sub>x</sub></i>S@C-400 anode was investigated by quantitatively studying the surface-controlled (capacitive) and diffusion-controlled charge storage contributions.<sup>[</sup><span><sup><a href="#smll202312190-bib-0049" class="bibLink tab-link" id="smll202312190-bib-0049_R_d30669543e1815" data-tab="pane-pcw-references" aria-label="Reference 49 - Nat. Commun.">49</a></sup></span><sup>]</sup> <b>Figure</b> <a href="#smll202312190-fig-0005">5a</a> showed the CV response at various sweep rates from 0.1 to 3&nbsp;mV&nbsp;s<sup>−1</sup>. The current intensity increased with increasing sweep rate, and the CV curves kept the original shape and became a bit broader at a high scan rate of 3&nbsp;mV&nbsp;s<sup>−1</sup>. The electrochemical reactions occurred on the Fe<sub>1-</sub><i><sub>x</sub></i>S@C-400 electrode involving the diffusion-controlled or the surface-controlled pseudocapacitive processes, which could be determined by the following equation:<sup>[</sup><span><sup><a href="#smll202312190-bib-0050" class="bibLink tab-link" id="smll202312190-bib-0050_R_d30669543e1836" data-tab="pane-pcw-references" aria-label="Reference 50 - Adv. Energy Mater.">50</a></sup></span><sup>]</sup>
            
            <div class="inline-equation" id="smll202312190-disp-0006"><span class="inline-equation__construct"><!--FIGURE-->
                  <span class="fallback__mathEquation" data-altimg="/cms/asset/22ca86cc-8076-4600-b6be-01dfe3b40d12/smll202312190-math-0006.png"></span><math altimg="urn:x-wiley:16136810:media:smll202312190:smll202312190-math-0006" display="block" location="graphic/smll202312190-math-0006.png">
                     <semantics>
                        <mrow>
                           <mi>log</mi>
                           <mo stretchy="false">(</mo>
                           <mi mathvariant="normal">i</mi>
                           <mo stretchy="false">)</mo>
                           <mspace width="0.33em"></mspace>
                           <mo linebreak="goodbreak">=</mo>
                           <mspace width="0.33em"></mspace>
                           <mi>blog</mi>
                           <mo stretchy="false">(</mo>
                           <mi mathvariant="normal">v</mi>
                           <mo stretchy="false">)</mo>
                           <mspace width="0.33em"></mspace>
                           <mo linebreak="goodbreak">+</mo>
                           <mspace width="0.33em"></mspace>
                           <mi>log</mi>
                           <mo stretchy="false">(</mo>
                           <mi mathvariant="normal">a</mi>
                           <mo stretchy="false">)</mo>
                        </mrow>
                        <annotation encoding="application/x-tex">$$\begin{equation}{\mathrm{log(i)\ = \ blog(v)\ + \ log(a)}}\end{equation}$$</annotation>
                     </semantics></math></span><span class="inline-equation__label">(6)</span></div>where a and b are two adjustable parameters. When the value of b is close to 0.5, represents an ionic diffusion-controlled process, and when it gets close to 1.0, indicating a surface-controlled pseudo-capacitance mechanism. Several cathodic/anodic peaks were chosen (labeled as Peak1, 2, 3, 4, 5, 6, and 7) to evaluate the relationship between logarithmic current <i>i</i>) and scan rate <i>v</i>). According to the linear relationships between log <i>i</i>) and log <i>v</i>) as shown in Figure&nbsp;<a href="#smll202312190-fig-0005">5b</a>, the obtained b values (slopes) of peaks 1, 2, 3, 4, 5, 6, and 7 were 0.83, 1.07, 0.92, 0.96, 1.04, 1.05, and 0.98, respectively, suggesting a pseudocapacitive-dominated behavior, and thus leading to excellent rate performance. The pseudocapacitive contribution was further calculated using the following equation:<sup>[</sup><span><sup><a href="#smll202312190-bib-0051" class="bibLink tab-link" id="smll202312190-bib-0051_R_d30669543e1892" data-tab="pane-pcw-references" aria-label="Reference 51 - ACS Nano">51</a></sup></span><sup>]</sup>
            
            <div class="inline-equation" id="smll202312190-disp-0007"><span class="inline-equation__construct"><!--FIGURE-->
                  <span class="fallback__mathEquation" data-altimg="/cms/asset/52841b5f-5549-4592-9d16-e3f897a98941/smll202312190-math-0007.png"></span><math altimg="urn:x-wiley:16136810:media:smll202312190:smll202312190-math-0007" display="block" location="graphic/smll202312190-math-0007.png">
                     <semantics>
                        <mrow>
                           <mi mathvariant="normal">i</mi>
                           <mo stretchy="false">(</mo>
                           <mi mathvariant="normal">V</mi>
                           <mo stretchy="false">)</mo>
                           <mspace width="0.33em"></mspace>
                           <mo linebreak="goodbreak">=</mo>
                           <mspace width="0.33em"></mspace>
                           <mi mathvariant="normal">k</mi>
                           <mn>1</mn>
                           <mi mathvariant="normal">v</mi>
                           <mo linebreak="goodbreak">+</mo>
                           <mi mathvariant="normal">k</mi>
                           <mn>2</mn>
                           <mi mathvariant="normal">v</mi>
                           <mn>1</mn>
                           <mo>/</mo>
                           <mn>2</mn>
                        </mrow>
                        <annotation encoding="application/x-tex">$$\begin{equation}{\mathrm{i(V)\ = \ k1v + k2v1/2}}\end{equation}$$</annotation>
                     </semantics></math></span><span class="inline-equation__label">(7)</span></div>where <i>i</i>(V) is the current at a fixed potential, k<sub>1</sub> and k<sub>2</sub> are adjustable parameters, k<sub>1</sub><i>v</i> and k<sub>2</sub><i>v</i><sup>1/2</sup> are pseudocapacitive and diffusion-controlled contributions, respectively. Thus, by determining k<sub>1</sub> and k<sub>2</sub> constants, the pseudocapacitive contributions at different sweep rates can be calculated. As depicted in Figure&nbsp;<a href="#smll202312190-fig-0005">5c</a>, along with increasing of sweep rate, it further increased and reached 95.3% at the sweep rate of 2&nbsp;mV&nbsp;s<sup>−1</sup> whilst the diffusion contribution gradually decreased. CV curves and corresponding capacitive proportion (ca. 81.5%, shaded area) at a sweep rate of 0.3&nbsp;mV&nbsp;s<sup>−1</sup> are depicted in Figure&nbsp;<a href="#smll202312190-fig-0005">5d</a>, and the rest of the capacity contribution profiles at other scan rates were displayed in Figure <a class="suppLink scrollableLink" href="#support-information-section">S12</a> (Supporting Information). As a consequence, the surface-controlled pseudocapacitive contribution was dominant in the whole charge storage process, especially at high sweep rates.<sup>[</sup><span><sup><a href="#smll202312190-bib-0052" class="bibLink tab-link" id="smll202312190-bib-0052_R_d30669543e1967" data-tab="pane-pcw-references" aria-label="Reference 52 - Chem. Eng. J.">52</a>, <a href="#smll202312190-bib-0053" class="bibLink tab-link" id="smll202312190-bib-0053_R_d30669543e1967" data-tab="pane-pcw-references" aria-label="Reference 53 - J. Solid State Electrochem.">53</a></sup></span><sup>]</sup></div>
         
         <section class="article-section__inline-figure">
            <figure class="figure" id="smll202312190-fig-0005"><a target="_blank" href="/cms/asset/89fdd6c4-4576-4b71-8432-c6dad3c07fb2/smll202312190-fig-0005-m.jpg"><picture>
                     <source srcset="/cms/asset/89fdd6c4-4576-4b71-8432-c6dad3c07fb2/smll202312190-fig-0005-m.jpg" media="(min-width: 1650px)"><img class="figure__image" src="/cms/asset/c84366e3-0aa4-473e-9e3c-3276f96f0af6/smll202312190-fig-0005-m.png" data-lg-src="/cms/asset/89fdd6c4-4576-4b71-8432-c6dad3c07fb2/smll202312190-fig-0005-m.jpg" alt="Details are in the caption following the image" title="Details are in the caption following the image" loading="lazy"></picture></a><figcaption class="figure__caption">
                  <div class="figure__caption__header"><strong class="figure__title">Figure 5<span style="font-weight:normal"></span></strong><div class="figure-extra"><a href="#" class="open-figure-link">Open in figure viewer</a><a href="/action/downloadFigures?id=smll202312190-fig-0005&amp;partId=&amp;doi=10.1002%2Fsmll.202312190" class="ppt-figure-link"><i aria-hidden="true" class="icon-Icon_Download"></i><span>PowerPoint</span></a></div>
                  </div>
                  <div class="figure__caption figure__caption-text">Kinetics investigation of the as-synthesized Fe<sub>1-</sub><i><sub>x</sub></i>S@C-400 composite. a) CV curves at various scan rates ranging from 0.1 to 3&nbsp;mV&nbsp;s<sup>−1</sup>. b) corresponding log i versus log v plots at each redox peak (peak current: i, scan rate: v). c) bar chart exhibiting the contribution ratio of pseudocapacitive contribution at various scan rates. d) CV curve with the pseudocapacitive contribution shown by the cyan region at a scan rate of 0.3&nbsp;mV&nbsp;s<sup>−1</sup>; e) First charge/discharge profile at 0.5&nbsp;A&nbsp;g<sup>−1</sup> with labeled points for in situ EIS; f) EIS spectra after different cycles; g) Na ion diffusion coefficients of the first two cycles at different discharge and charge state of Fe<sub>1-</sub><i><sub>x</sub></i>S@C composites.</div>
               </figcaption>
            </figure>
         </section>
         <p>In situ electrochemical impedance spectroscopy (In situ EIS) during the initial discharge–charge cycle was carried out to study the electrochemical reaction kinetics differences induced by pulverization and phase transition of active materials at different sodiation-desodiation stages. Figure&nbsp;<a href="#smll202312190-fig-0005">5e</a> exhibits the EIS spectra of the Fe<sub>1-</sub><i><sub>x</sub></i>S@C-400 electrode in the first discharge–charge cycle at various states. The Nyquist plots were composed of at least one depressed semicircle in the high- and middle-frequency range and an inclined line at low frequency, which agreed with the previous report. At the open-circuit voltage (OCV) state, the semicircle in the high-frequency region was related to the charge-transfer resistance (Rct), which resulted from the poor electrical conductivity of the active materials, and the inclined line in the low-frequency region was ascribed to the Warburg impedance (W) associated with the diffusion coefficient of Na<sup>+</sup> at the interface between the electrode and the electrolyte.<sup>[</sup><span><sup><a href="#smll202312190-bib-0054" class="bibLink tab-link" id="smll202312190-bib-0054_R_d30669543e2018" data-tab="pane-pcw-references" aria-label="Reference 54 - J. Electrochem. Sci. Technol.">54</a></sup></span><sup>]</sup> However, at other states, the semicircle corresponded to the mutual effect of SEI film resistance (<i>R</i><sub>SEI</sub>) and Rct.<sup>[</sup><span><sup><a href="#smll202312190-bib-0055" class="bibLink tab-link" id="smll202312190-bib-0055_R_d30669543e2027" data-tab="pane-pcw-references" aria-label="Reference 55 - Electrochim. Acta">55</a></sup></span><sup>]</sup> In general, the resistance increased obviously from OCV to 0.01&nbsp;V because of the formation of a nonconductive sodium sulfide matrix and SEI films and volume change.<sup>[</sup><span><sup><a href="#smll202312190-bib-0056" class="bibLink tab-link" id="smll202312190-bib-0056_R_d30669543e2032" data-tab="pane-pcw-references" aria-label="Reference 56 - Small">56</a></sup></span><sup>]</sup> However, an unexpected decreasing resistance phenomenon was observed during the discharge cycle, which could be ascribed to the pulverization of Fe<sub>1-</sub><i><sub>x</sub></i>S@C-400 with more exposed metallic Fe<sup>0</sup>. During the charge cycle, the Na<i><sub>y</sub></i>Fe<sub>1-</sub><i><sub>x</sub></i>S and Fe<sub>1-</sub><i><sub>x</sub></i>S phase gradually increased and insulative sodium sulfide gradually decreased. Thereby, the resistance decreased gradually from 0.01 to 3.0&nbsp;V. In addition, EIS tests were also measured after various cycles at a current density of 20&nbsp;A&nbsp;g<sup>−1</sup> to show the charge-transfer stability. With the increasing number of cycles, the resistance of the Fe<sub>1-</sub><i><sub>x</sub></i>S electrode gradually increased (Figure&nbsp;<a href="#smll202312190-fig-0005">5f</a>).</p>
         
         <div class="paragraph-element">Moreover, the Galvanostatic intermittent titration technique (GITT) was further carried out to study the influence of multistep sodiation and desodiation reactions of Fe<sub>1-</sub><i><sub>x</sub></i>S@C-400 composite on sodium-ion diffusion coefficient. The ion diffusivity D<sub>Na</sub> can be obtained by following the formula:<sup>[</sup><span><sup><a href="#smll202312190-bib-0057" class="bibLink tab-link" id="smll202312190-bib-0057_R_d30669543e2074" data-tab="pane-pcw-references" aria-label="Reference 57 - Chem. Eng. J.">57</a></sup></span><sup>]</sup>
            
            <div class="inline-equation" id="smll202312190-disp-0008"><span class="inline-equation__construct"><!--FIGURE-->
                  <span class="fallback__mathEquation" data-altimg="/cms/asset/ff8274b1-8e58-4fd4-bcb1-5b2df2259738/smll202312190-math-0008.png"></span><math altimg="urn:x-wiley:16136810:media:smll202312190:smll202312190-math-0008" display="block" location="graphic/smll202312190-math-0008.png">
                     <semantics>
                        <mrow>
                           <mrow>
                              <mi>DNa</mi>
                              <mspace width="0.33em"></mspace>
                           </mrow>
                           <mo linebreak="badbreak">=</mo>
                           <mfrac>
                              <mn>4</mn>
                              <mrow>
                                 <mi>π</mi>
                                 <mi mathvariant="normal">Δ</mi>
                                 <mi>τ</mi>
                              </mrow>
                           </mfrac>
                           <mspace width="0.33em"></mspace>
                           <mfenced close=")" open="(" separators="">
                              <mfrac>
                                 <mrow>
                                    <msub>
                                       <mi>m</mi>
                                       <mi>B</mi>
                                    </msub>
                                    <msub>
                                       <mi>V</mi>
                                       <mi>M</mi>
                                    </msub>
                                 </mrow>
                                 <mrow>
                                    <msub>
                                       <mi>M</mi>
                                       <mi>B</mi>
                                    </msub>
                                    <mi>S</mi>
                                 </mrow>
                              </mfrac>
                           </mfenced>
                           <msup>
                              <mfenced close=")" open="(" separators="">
                                 <mfrac>
                                    <mrow>
                                       <mi mathvariant="normal">Δ</mi>
                                       <msub>
                                          <mi>E</mi>
                                          <mi>S</mi>
                                       </msub>
                                    </mrow>
                                    <mrow>
                                       <mi mathvariant="normal">Δ</mi>
                                       <msub>
                                          <mi>E</mi>
                                          <mi>τ</mi>
                                       </msub>
                                    </mrow>
                                 </mfrac>
                              </mfenced>
                              <mn>2</mn>
                           </msup>
                           <mspace width="0.33em"></mspace>
                        </mrow>
                        <annotation encoding="application/x-tex">$$\begin{equation}{\mathrm{DNa\ }} = \frac{4}{{\pi \Delta \tau }}\ \left( {\frac{{{{m}_B}{{V}_M}}}{{{{M}_B}S}}} \right){{\left( {\frac{{\Delta {{E}_S}}}{{\Delta {{E}_\tau }}}} \right)}^2}\ \end{equation}$$</annotation>
                     </semantics></math></span><span class="inline-equation__label">(8)</span></div>Where τ, m<sub>B</sub>, V<sub>M</sub>, M<sub>B</sub>, S, ΔE<sub>s</sub>, and ΔE<sub>τ</sub> represent the duration of the current impulse, the mass load of the electrode material, the molar volume of the materials, molar weight, geometric area of the electrode, quasi-thermodynamic equilibrium potential difference between before and after the current pulse, and voltage change caused by pulse, respectively. Figure <a class="suppLink scrollableLink" href="#support-information-section">S13</a> (Supporting Information) showes a typically amplified titration, different parameters (ΔE<sub>s</sub>, and ΔE<sub>τ</sub>, etc.), and the well-fitted line among the voltage (V) and duration time (t) in this single process. Note that <i>E</i><sub>o</sub> induced by the current pulse was not counted in ΔE<sub>τ</sub> for discharge and charge GITT. Considering the pulverization process occurred in the initial cycle, the first two discharge/charge processes were recorded, as shown in Figure <a class="suppLink scrollableLink" href="#support-information-section">S14a</a> (Supporting Information). The Na-ion diffusion coefficients of the Fe<sub>1-</sub><i><sub>x</sub></i>S@C-400 anode at different discharge and charge states were calculated and plotted in Figure&nbsp;<a href="#smll202312190-fig-0005">5g</a> and compared with those of the Fe<sub>1-</sub><i><sub>x</sub></i>S@C-500 anode. The corresponding sodium diffusion coefficients of Fe<sub>1-</sub><i><sub>x</sub></i>S@C-400 were higher than those of Fe<sub>1-</sub><i><sub>x</sub></i>S@C-500. This was mainly attributed to the ultrafine pulverization of Fe<sub>1-</sub><i><sub>x</sub></i>S@C-400 composite, which has a higher ionic conductivity compared with Fe<sub>1-</sub><i><sub>x</sub></i>S@C-500. The D<sub>Na</sub> varying tendencies of the first two cycles were similar during the sodiation and desodiation, and the Na-ion diffusion coefficient of the Fe<sub>1-</sub><i><sub>x</sub></i>S@C-400 electrode has a value between 1.71&nbsp;×&nbsp;10<sup>−13</sup> and 1.60&nbsp;×&nbsp;10<sup>−10&nbsp;</sup>cm<sup>2</sup>&nbsp;s<sup>−1</sup>. Note that the minimum values at the total discharge state represent the deep diffusion of Na<sup>+</sup> ions in the anode. It was reasonable to assume that the surface of carbon was easier to capture Na-ion than the inner part. As the surface-active sites were gradually occupied, Na-ion began to insert into the carbon. However, the Na-ion had to overcome the repulsion force from the adsorbed Na-ion that could lead to a remarkable reduction in D<sub>Na</sub>. With the insertion length increasing, the D<sub>Na</sub> gradually becomes lower and lower.<sup>[</sup><span><sup><a href="#smll202312190-bib-0049" class="bibLink tab-link" id="smll202312190-bib-0049_R_d30669543e2210" data-tab="pane-pcw-references" aria-label="Reference 49 - Nat. Commun.">49</a></sup></span><sup>]</sup> Accordingly, it exhibited high D<sub>Na</sub> values at the starting charge process, and then gradually reduced. The average D<sub>Na</sub> values of Fe<sub>1-</sub><i><sub>x</sub></i>S@C-400 at the first discharge and charge plateaus were ≈2.29&nbsp;×&nbsp;10<sup>−12</sup> and 6.93&nbsp;×&nbsp;10<sup>−12</sup>&nbsp;cm<sup>2</sup>&nbsp;s<sup>−1</sup>, respectively. The average D<sub>Na</sub> values at the second discharge and charge plateaus were ≈5.01&nbsp;×&nbsp;10<sup>−12</sup> and 4.98&nbsp;×&nbsp;10<sup>−12&nbsp;</sup>cm<sup>2</sup>&nbsp;s<sup>−1</sup>, respectively. While the average D<sub>Na</sub> values at the first and second charge processes shared similar values at each state, indicating the pulverization process mainly occurred during the initial discharge process and the stability of the electrode after pulverization. Furthermore, the third cycle GITT curve was also recorded to compare with the initial two cycles, and the Na-ion diffusion coefficients at the third discharge and charge states were calculated and plotted in Figure <a class="suppLink scrollableLink" href="#support-information-section">S14b</a> (Supporting Information). It can be seen that the average D<sub>Na</sub> values at the third discharge–charge processes achieved comparable values at each state with that of the second discharge–charge processes, which further implied the superior stability of the Fe<sub>1-</sub><i><sub>x</sub></i>S@C anode after the initial cycle.</div>
         
         <p>DFT calculations were conducted to get further insight into the impressive electrochemical performance of the Fe<sub>1-</sub><i><sub>x</sub></i>S@C-400 anode. Here, we considered that the initial state of Fe<sub>1-</sub><i><sub>x</sub></i>S nanoparticles (denoted as FS) is defect-free, while the nanocrystal is defective after the pulverization (denoted as FS-v), and both crystal models were constructed and displayed in Figure <a class="suppLink scrollableLink" href="#support-information-section">S15</a> (Supporting Information). First, the adsorption energies (<i>E</i><sub>ads</sub>) between Na ion and the surface of FS and FS-v were calculated. Figure <a class="suppLink scrollableLink" href="#support-information-section">S16</a> (Supporting Information) displayed the Na adsorbed on the surface of FS and FS-v (top view and side view). <b>Figure</b> <a href="#smll202312190-fig-0006">6a,b</a> presents the 3D charge density differences of single Na atom adsorbed on the surface FS and FS-v, respectively, where the electron-rich and hole-rich regions are distributing obviously, and the charge accumulation (greenish-yellow parts) and charge depletion (cyan parts) revealed the charge transfer from Na<sup>+</sup> to FS and FS-v. For Na/FS-v system, the charge accumulation was observed not only between the Na atom and FS-v interface but also between the Na atom and vacancies. The FS-v surface possessed a larger amount of charge accumulation than that of the FS surface, indicating a stronger binding energy between Na<sup>+</sup> and FS-v. This result was further confirmed through the adsorption energy calculation. The <i>E</i><sub>ads</sub> values of a single Na ion on FS and FS-v surface were −1.725 and −2.157&nbsp;eV, respectively. It demonstrated that the existence of vacancies could enhance the Na<sup>+</sup> adsorption ability of Fe<sub>1-</sub><i><sub>x</sub></i>S. Second, the migration energy barrier was also calculated to evaluate the Na-ion transport. Figure&nbsp;<a href="#smll202312190-fig-0006">6c</a> displays the Na ion diffusion path and energy barriers on both surfaces of FS and FS-v. It was obvious that the energy barriers for FS-v were lower than those for FS, manifesting that the defects could facilitate the Na-ion diffusion kinetics. Finally, the adsorption energies between nanoparticles (FS and FS-v) and carbon substrate were also calculated to further understand the non-aggregation phenomenon after the pulverization process. In general, nanosized particles tend to aggregate during the electrochemical sodiation/desodiation process, resulting in an inevitable capacity decay. Surprisingly, the aggregation phenomenon after this ultrafine pulverization process did not happen in subsequent cycling. It was speculated that the pulverized Fe<sub>1-</sub><i><sub>x</sub></i>S nanoparticles attached to or embedded in a carbon matrix and thus avoided the aggregation. To get a deep understanding of the above phenomenon, the surface chemical bond between carbon and FS-v nanoparticles was further investigated by DFT calculation. The adsorption energies (<i>E</i><sub>ads</sub>) calculated between carbon and the surface of FS and FS-v were −1.715 and −2.836&nbsp;eV, respectively, exhibiting more negative adsorption energy after pulverization (Figure&nbsp;<a href="#smll202312190-fig-0006">6d,e</a>). Based on the experiment finding and theoretical calculation, it was speculated that the pulverized Fe<sub>1-</sub><i><sub>x</sub></i>S ultrafine nanoparticles attached to or embedded in a carbon matrix and thus avoided aggregation, and the more negative adsorption energy between carbon and FeS-V was more beneficial to the fixation of ultrafine nanoparticles on the surface of carbon, thereby effectively avoiding aggregation during repeated discharge/charge process. Consequently, the Fe<sub>1-</sub><i><sub>x</sub></i>S@C simultaneously exhibited high reversible capacity, superior rate capability, and ultralong cycling stability.</p>
         
         <section class="article-section__inline-figure">
            <figure class="figure" id="smll202312190-fig-0006"><a target="_blank" href="/cms/asset/21b0d8d5-3c23-4ef0-9a97-35f92df04ac1/smll202312190-fig-0006-m.jpg"><picture>
                     <source srcset="/cms/asset/21b0d8d5-3c23-4ef0-9a97-35f92df04ac1/smll202312190-fig-0006-m.jpg" media="(min-width: 1650px)"><img class="figure__image" src="/cms/asset/2afd5a54-f375-4390-a668-2255acc7f5b3/smll202312190-fig-0006-m.png" data-lg-src="/cms/asset/21b0d8d5-3c23-4ef0-9a97-35f92df04ac1/smll202312190-fig-0006-m.jpg" alt="Details are in the caption following the image" title="Details are in the caption following the image" loading="lazy"></picture></a><figcaption class="figure__caption">
                  <div class="figure__caption__header"><strong class="figure__title">Figure 6<span style="font-weight:normal"></span></strong><div class="figure-extra"><a href="#" class="open-figure-link">Open in figure viewer</a><a href="/action/downloadFigures?id=smll202312190-fig-0006&amp;partId=&amp;doi=10.1002%2Fsmll.202312190" class="ppt-figure-link"><i aria-hidden="true" class="icon-Icon_Download"></i><span>PowerPoint</span></a></div>
                  </div>
                  <div class="figure__caption figure__caption-text">Top view and side view of the charge density differences and the corresponding adsorbed energies with one Na atom adsorbed on a) FS surface and b) FS-v surface, greenish yellow, and cyan areas represent the charge accumulation and loss, respectively; c) Na-ion migration path (top view and side view) and diffusion energy barriers on FS and FS-v surface; Top view, side view, and the corresponding adsorbed energies of the optimized geometries for the interaction and bonding between carbon and Fe<sub>1-</sub><i><sub>x</sub></i>S: d) carbon with FS surface and e) carbon with FS-v surface.</div>
               </figcaption>
            </figure>
         </section>
      </section>
      <section class="article-section__content" id="smll202312190-sec-0030">
         
         <h2 class="article-section__title section__title section1" id="smll202312190-sec-0030-title">3 Conclusion</h2>
         
         <p>In summary, ultrathin Fe<sub>1-</sub><i><sub>x</sub></i>S@C nanoplates have been prepared successfully via a facile coating-carbonation-sulfidation strategy. When used as an anode material for SIBs, an interesting ultrafine pulverization phenomenon of the Fe<sub>1-</sub><i><sub>x</sub></i>S@C anode during the first discharge was observed, and the Fe<sub>1-</sub><i><sub>x</sub></i>S@C nanoplates were completely pulverized into ultrafine particles with quantum size (≈ 5&nbsp;nm) and no discernable aggregation was detected in subsequent cycles. In situ XRD and Raman demonstrated that the pulverized ultrafine particles can significantly overcome the kinetic and thermodynamic limitations of the conversion reaction, realizing the highly reversible conversion reaction of Fe<sub>1-</sub><i><sub>x</sub></i>S. Additionally, the kinetics analysis revealed that the capacity contribution was dominated by capacitive behavior. DFT calculations further deciphered that the pulverization of ultrathin carbon-coated Fe<sub>1-</sub><i><sub>x</sub></i>S nanoplates could not only significantly reduce both the adsorbed energies and diffusion energy barriers of Na atom but also effectively prevent the aggregation of Fe<sub>1-</sub><i><sub>x</sub></i>S particles by strengthening the adsorption between pulverized Fe<sub>1-</sub><i><sub>x</sub></i>S nanoparticles and carbon. Benefiting from the unique ultrafine pulverization, the Fe<sub>1-</sub><i><sub>x</sub></i>S@C anode simultaneously exhibited high reversible capacity (610&nbsp;mAh&nbsp;g<sup>−1</sup> at 500&nbsp;mA&nbsp;g<sup>−1</sup>), and excellent rate capability (427.9&nbsp;mAh&nbsp;g<sup>−1</sup> at 20&nbsp;A&nbsp;g<sup>−1</sup>), and long-term cycle stability (377.9&nbsp;mAh&nbsp;g<sup>−1</sup> after 2500&nbsp;cycles at 20&nbsp;A&nbsp;g<sup>−1</sup>). This work holds a meaningful insight into the nanomaterial engineering strategies and pulverization phenomenon and might suggest a possible way to design advanced electrode materials for energy storage devices.</p>
         </section>
      <div class="article-section__content">
